Innistrad Championship Historic Metagame Breakdown
==================================================



 Posted in [NEWS](/en/articles)
 on December 3, 2021 






![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/styles/auth_small/public/images/person/authorpic_FrankKarsten.jpg)
By Frank Karsten











The [Innistrad Championship](https://magic.gg/events/innistrad-championship) is underway now! With members of the *Magic* Pro League and the *Magic* Rivals League as well as top players from qualifying events held on *MTG Arena* and *Magic Online*, they battle for $450,000 in prizes in both Standard and Historic formats live December 3–5 at [twitch.tv/magic](https://www.twitch.tv/magic).


You can [find the Innistrad Championship decklists online now](https://magic.gg/news/innistrad-championship-standard-and-historic-decklists), with examples of every archetype included below to see what's being played across the tournament. This article covers Historic, but [the Standard breakdown has all the same details ready for you](https://magic.gg/news/innistrad-championship-standard-metagame-breakdown).


Historic Metagame Breakdown
===========================


This article expands on [the Innistrad Championship metagame preview](https://magic.gg/news/innistrad-championship-metagame-preview), diving into the decklists and analyzing what to expect throughout the weekend. Friday and Saturday feature a combined seven rounds of (best-of-three) Historic. In addition, Sunday's Top 8 double-elimination playoff is exclusively Historic.


![](https://images.ctfassets.net/ryplwhabvmmk/79LJYoYwhD2lSdiuspL382/0572a35595f6dcbe7292dbbce4eb5fbd/1920x1080-Innistrad-Championship-Historic-Metagame.jpg)




| Archetype | Count | % Field |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Selesnya Humans | 41 | 16.3% |
| Izzet Phoenix | 34 | 13.5% |

Like Standard, Historic has recently seen the influx of *Innistrad: Midnight Hunt* and *Innistrad: Crimson Vow*. But in addition, Historic also saw the release of *Jumpstart: Historic Horizons* and the suspension of [Memory Lapse](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Memory+Lapse) in the last few months. As a result, the metagame has transformed, and the *Innistrad* Championship is one of the first major *Magic* events to showcase for Historic since the start of all these changes.


Looking at the metagame, it's exciting to see a large amount of diversity. The most-played cards overall are [Collected Company](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Collected+Company), [Expressive Iteration](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Expressive+Iteration), [Thoughtseize](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize), and [Fatal Push](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fatal+Push), which have been format staples for quite a while. But it's undeniable that the last three sets have reinvigorated the format. Let me give a quick overview of all newly added cards with at least 90 copies across all Historic main decks and sideboards at the *Innistrad* Championship. (To put that number into perspective: each of these cards is played by at least 10% of the competitors.)


* [![Unholy Heat](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Unholy+Heat)](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unholy+Heat)
* [![522088](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&multiverseid=522088)](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?multiverseid=522088)
* [![Archmage's Charm](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Archmage%27s+Charm)](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Archmage%27s+Charm)
* [![Thalia's Lieutenant](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Thalia%27s+Lieutenant)](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thalia%27s+Lieutenant)
* [![Dragon's Rage Channeler](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Dragon%27s+Rage+Channeler)](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dragon%27s+Rage+Channeler)
* [![Ranger-Captain of Eos](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Ranger-Captain+of+Eos)](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ranger-Captain+of+Eos)
* [![522287](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&multiverseid=522287)](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?multiverseid=522287)
* [![Scurry Oak](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Scurry+Oak)](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scurry+Oak)

*Jumpstart: Historic Horizons* introduced an abundance of cards that elevated various archetypes to competitive viability:


* [Unholy Heat](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unholy+Heat), at 244 copies in total, is the most-played of the bunch. The powerful removal spell already was a Modern staple, so it's not surprising that it has been adopted by wide variety of red decks in Historic. It excels in decks like Izzet Phoenix, Rakdos Arcanist, or Mono-Red Madness where delirium can be achieved reliably. In these archetypes, another Modern staple in Dragon's Rage Channeler has also found a home.
* [Esper Sentinel](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Esper+Sentinel), Thalia's Lieutenant, and [Ranger-Captain of Eos](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ranger-Captain+of+Eos) gave a big boost to the Humans tribe. Selesnya Humans is now the most-played Historic archetype, and it's all thanks to these additions. Some Humans also found homes in other archetypes—[Esper Sentinel](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Esper+Sentinel) reduces the cost of affinity spells in Azorius Affinity, and [Ranger-Captain of Eos](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ranger-Captain+of+Eos) can fetch [Soul Warden](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Soul+Warden) in Heliod Company.
* Archmage's Charm is yet another Modern staple that has found widespread adoption in Historic. It's tough on the mana base, but it's flexible, powerful, and a control player's dream. The card is most prominently found in all Jeskai Control, Izzet Epiphany, and Dimir Control decks.
* [Ravenous Squirrel](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ravenous+Squirrel) has become Cauldron Familiar's best friend, and it has been adopted by almost every Golgari Food, Jund Food, and Jund Company player.
* [Scurry Oak](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scurry+Oak) yields an infinite-life combo when combined with [Heliod, Sun-Crowned](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Heliod%2C+Sun-Crowned) and [Soul Warden](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Soul+Warden). In the process, you're also creating infinite power and toughness. Packed in a [Collected Company](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Collected+Company) shell, the resulting Heliod Company archetype is the third-most popular Historic archetype at the Innistrad Championship.

* [![Consider](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Consider)](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consider)
* [![Brutal Cathar](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Brutal+Cathar)](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brutal+Cathar)
* [![534886](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&multiverseid=534886)](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?multiverseid=534886)

*Innistrad: Midnight Hunt*' “s most important Historic addition, judging by the total number of copies registered for the Innistrad Championship, was [Consider](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consider). The cantrip is perfect for Izzet Phoenix as a way to either mill or return [Arclight Phoenix](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arclight+Phoenix). In part due to the introduction of [Consider](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consider), Izzet Phoenix has become the second-most popular Historic archetype.


Another relevant addition was [Brutal Cathar](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brutal+Cathar), which has the right mix of creature types, mana value, and disruption to slot right into Selesnya Humans.


Finally, [The Meathook Massacre](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=The+Meathook+Massacre) encouraged many [Cauldron Familiar](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cauldron+Familiar) afficionados to drop the red and switch to Golgari Food. Red offers [Korvold, Fae-Cursed King](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Korvold%2C+Fae-Cursed+King) and [Mayhem Devil](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mayhem+Devil), but [The Meathook Massacre](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=The+Meathook+Massacre) can be just as powerful against opposing creature decks. If things go right, it sweeps their entire board while a huge [Ravenous Squirrel](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ravenous+Squirrel) on your side survives. Even more importantly, [The Meathook Massacre](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=The+Meathook+Massacre) has mana value two, which opens up Lurrus of the Dream-Den as a companion. All Golgari Food decks had Lurrus as their companion, and it's the fourth most-played Historic archetype at the Innistrad Championship.


* [![541141](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&multiverseid=541141)](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?multiverseid=541141)
* [![540879](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&multiverseid=540879)](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?multiverseid=540879)
* [![Flame-Blessed Bolt](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Flame-Blessed+Bolt)](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flame-Blessed+Bolt)

*Innistrad: Crimson Vow* offered [Stormcarved Coast](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stormcarved+Coast) and [Flame-Blessed Bolt](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Flame-Blessed+Bolt) to decks like Izzet Phoenix and Izzet Epiphany, but these are basically minor upgrades of already existing effects.


[Voice of the Blessed](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Voice+of+the+Blessed), the final major addition, could be seen as an upgrade to the already existing [Trelasarra, Moon Dancer](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trelasarra%2C+Moon+Dancer), but it's usually played in addition rather than instead. Moreover, thanks to [Soul Warden](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Soul+Warden), a Heliod Company player can easily put four +1/+1 counters on [Voice of the Blessed](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Voice+of+the+Blessed) and fly over for the win, which provides a solid game plan if you don't draw all the combo pieces.

**Selesnya Humans (41 players)**: These decks curve out early with [Esper Sentinel](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Esper+Sentinel) into [Thalia's Lieutenant](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thalia%27s+Lieutenant) and have an awesome collection of three-mana creatures to hit with [Collected Company](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Collected+Company). [Elite Spellbinder](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elite+Spellbinder) is a frequently-played one, but it's not a universal inclusion. Roughly a quarter of Selesnya Humans players are experimenting with *Innistrad: Crimson Vow's* [Hamlet Vanguard](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hamlet+Vanguard).

75 Cards 




![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Scurry+Oak)

















**Heliod Company (26 players)**: When [Scurry Oak](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scurry+Oak) enters the battlefield, [Soul Warden](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Soul+Warden) gains a life, which in turn triggers Heliod to put a +1/+1 counter on [Scurry Oak](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scurry+Oak). [Scurry Oak](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scurry+Oak) then creates a token, and you can loop this as often as you like.

[The Meathook Massacre](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BThe%5D+%5BMeathook%5D+%5BMassacre%5D)


75 Cards 




![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Cauldron+Familiar)

















**Golgari Food (21 players)**: The trio of [Cauldron Familiar](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cauldron+Familiar), Witch's Oven, and [Trail of Crumbs](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trail+of+Crumbs) has remained a powerful core ever since the inception of the Historic format. In Golgari Food, they are joined by [Ravenous Squirrel](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ravenous+Squirrel) and [The Meathook Massacre](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=The+Meathook+Massacre) in a low-curve, two-color deck that exploits Lurrus of the Dream-Den as the companion.








#### Floch, Ivan - Jeskai Control


#####

![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Teferi%2C+Hero+of+Dominaria)

















**Jeskai Control (18 players)**: [Archmage's Charm](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Archmage%27s+Charm) and [Lightning Helix](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Helix) deal with anything the opponent might attempt, and [Teferi, Hero of Dominaria](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Teferi%2C+Hero+of+Dominaria) will win the game in the end. Slightly over half of the Jeskai Control decks also have the potential to cast Magma Opus from the graveyard with [Torrential Gearhulk](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Torrential+Gearhulk).

![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Korvold%2C+Fae-Cursed+King)

















**Jund Food (16 players)**: Most versions have adopted [Ravenous Squirrel](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ravenous+Squirrel), but apart from that, decklists look very similar to lists from a year ago. Then again, [Gilded Goose](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gilded+Goose) ramping into [Mayhem Devil](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mayhem+Devil) and [Korvold, Fae-Cursed King](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Korvold%2C+Fae-Cursed+King) is still as strong as ever.

![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Sorin+the+Mirthless)

















**Rakdos Arcanist (13 players)**: An ideal curve would start with [Thoughtseize](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize), [Inquisition of Kozilek](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek), or [Unholy Heat](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unholy+Heat) on turn one, followed by [Dreadhorde Arcanist](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dreadhorde+Arcanist) on turn two. An escaped [Kroxa, Titan of Death's Hunger](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kroxa%2C+Titan+of+Death%27s+Hunger) will seal the deal.

75 Cards 




![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Korvold%2C+Fae-Cursed+King)

















**Jund Citadel (10 players)**: When you see [Gilded Goose](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gilded+Goose) and [Mayhem Devil](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mayhem+Devil), you might expect [Cauldron Familiar](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cauldron+Familiar) or Witch's Oven, but nearly all Jund Citadel players cut the Cat-Oven combo. Instead, their card choices are geared towards ramping into Bolas's Citadel as quickly as possible. Once the artifact is on the battlefield, you can usually cast an absurdly large number of spells from the top without paying their mana cost, while regaining some life with [Prosperous Innkeeper](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Prosperous+Innkeeper).

![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Niv-Mizzet%2C+Parun)

















**Izzet Epiphany (9 players)**: If it works in Standard, then why not in Historic? [Unexpected Windfall](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Unexpected+Windfall), [Galvanic Iteration](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Galvanic+Iteration), [Alrund's Epiphany](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Alrund%27s+Epiphany) are legal in Historic as well, and it's even better when you can support them with powerful spells like Archmage's Charm.

75 Cards 




![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=The+Locust+God)

















**Izzet Creativity (6 players)**: [Hard Evidence](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hard+Evidence) conveniently provides two targets for [Indomitable Creativity](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Indomitable+Creativity), and when an Izzet Creativity player casts it for X=2, they should hit the only two creatures in the deck: [The Locust God](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=The+Locust+God) and Sage of Falls. Together, they'll immediately create a game-winning number of 1/1 hasted fliers.

4
[Niv-Mizzet Reborn](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BNiv-Mizzet%5D+%5BReborn%5D)


1
[The Scarab God](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BThe%5D+%5BScarab%5D+%5BGod%5D)


75 Cards 




![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Niv-Mizzet+Reborn)

















**Five-Color Niv-Mizzet (5 players)**: Pretty much every spell in this deck is multicolored in order to maximize [Niv-Mizzet Reborn](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Niv-Mizzet+Reborn). The Triome-heavy mana base required to support Niv-Mizzet also supports [Territorial Kavu](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Territorial+Kavu) perfectly—a 5/5 on turn two is not out of the question!

75 Cards 




![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Thought+Monitor)

















**Azorius Affinity (5 players)**: This deck is not as hyper-aggressive as old-school Modern Affinity—the prevalent Historic version is grindier and more interactive—but the name is adequate. Indeed, the deck features the actual affinity mechanic on [Thought Monitor](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thought+Monitor), an actual artifact land in [Treasure Vault](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Treasure+Vault), and a mix between [Cranial Plating](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cranial+Plating) and [Master of Etherium](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Master+of+Etherium) in the form of [Nettlecyst](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nettlecyst).

![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Hullbreaker+Horror)

















**Dimir Control (5 players)**: There's quite a bit of variability across the specific card choices, but the overall control plan is clear. [Archmage's Charm](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Archmage%27s+Charm) and [Fatal Push](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fatal+Push) deal with anything the opponent might attempt, and [Shark Typhoon](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shark+Typhoon) will win the game in the end.

![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Chandra%2C+Torch+of+Defiance)

















**Mono-Red Madness (5 players)**: The dream is to cast [Faithless Looting](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Faithless+Looting) on turn one, discarding two copies of [Blazing Rootwalla](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blazing+Rootwalla). [Dragon's Rage Channeler](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dragon%27s+Rage+Channeler) is a powerful one-drop as well. Interesting to note is that most players eschewed [Magmatic Channeler](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Magmatic+Channeler), opting for versions with [Hollow One](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hollow+One) or [Bonecrusher Giant](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bonecrusher+Giant) instead.

**Azorius Auras (4 players)**: [Kor Spiritdancer](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kor+Spiritdancer) and [Sram, Senior Edificer](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sram%2C+Senior+Edificer) will trigger when you're suiting up your creatures with [Sentinel's Eyes](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sentinel%27s+Eyes), [Staggering Insight](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Staggering+Insight), and so on.

75 Cards 




![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Bladewing+the+Risen)

















**Dragonstorm (4 players)**: This awesome new build of Dragonstorm can discard the nine-mana sorcery with [Faithless Looting](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Faithless+Looting) or Faithless Mending, then flash it back with [Mizzix's Mastery](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mizzix%27s+Mastery), grab [Terror of the Peaks](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terror+of+the+Peaks) and 2 [Bladewing the Risen](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bladewing+the+Risen), and deal infinite damage. If you don't draw Dragonstorm, you can discard [Emergent Ultimatum](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emergent+Ultimatum) instead. A game-winning Ultimatum package is Dragonstorm, [Solve the Equation](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Solve+the+Equation), and [Omniscience](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Omniscience).

##### Mythic (7)



3
[Serra's Emissary](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BSerra%5D+%5BEmissary%5D)


4
[Indomitable Creativity](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BIndomitable%5D+%5BCreativity%5D)


75 Cards 




![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Serra%27s+Emissary)

















**Jeskai Creativity (4 players)**: An [Indomitable Creativity](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Indomitable+Creativity) for X=1 will reliably put [Serra's Emissary](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Serra%27s+Emissary) onto the battlefield. Many creature decks have difficulty beating an opponent who has protection from creatures.

![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Sanctum+Weaver)

















**Selesnya Enchantress (2 players)**: [Sythis, Harvest's Hand](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sythis%2C+Harvest%27s+Hand) and [Enchantress's Presence](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Enchantress%27s+Presence) will trigger when you're casting enchantments like [Sterling Grove](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sterling+Grove) or [Sanctum Weaver](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sanctum+Weaver). One of the two players has the [Solemnity](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Solemnity) – [Nine Lives](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nine+Lives) combo as well.

**Elves (2 players)**: The dream curve would be [Llanowar Elves](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Llanowar+Elves) on turn one, [Elvish Archdruid](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Archdruid) on turn two, followed by some combination of [Elvish Warmaster](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Warmaster), [Imperious Perfect](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Imperious+Perfect), and/or [Collected Company](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Collected+Company) on turn three.

**Rakdos Goblins (2 players)**: [Muxus, Goblin Grandee](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Muxus%2C+Goblin+Grandee) and [Krenko, Mob Boss](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krenko%2C+Mob+Boss) have spearheaded the Goblin tribe since the inception of the Historic format, and recently *Jumpstart: Historic Horizons* has introduced [Munitions Expert](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Munitions+Expert) as an additional reason to splash black.

**Simic Merfolk (1 player)**: A classic tribal deck, Simic Merfolk uses lords like [Merfolk Mistbinder](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Merfolk+Mistbinder) to beef up creatures, along with [Svyelun of Sea and Sky](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Svyelun+of+Sea+and+Sky) and [Collected Company](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Collected+Company) to generate card advantage.

75 Cards 




![](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Ox+of+Agonas)

















**Mono-Red Storm (1 player)**: When you control [Birgi, God of Storytelling](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birgi%2C+God+of+Storytelling), you can bounce and recast [Grinning Ignus](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grinning+Ignus) as often as you like. If you also control [Hazoret's Monument](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hazoret%27s+Monument), then that's infinite loots, allowing you to find [Grapeshot](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grapeshot) for the win.

**Azorius Lotus Field (1 player)**: [Lotus Field](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotus+Field) requires a steep sacrifice, but [Stifle](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stifle) and [Discontinuity](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Discontinuity) can negate it. This allows you to ramp into [Hullbreaker Horror](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hullbreaker+Horror) or a massive Sphinx's [Revelation](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Revelation) quickly.

**Jeskai Lotus Field (1 player)**: There are many similarities and differences with Azorius Lotus Field, but one thing to point out is that the detrimental enters-the-battlefield trigger of [Lotus Field](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lotus+Field) is also stopped by [Strict Proctor](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Strict+Proctor).

**Mono-Red Aggro (1 player)**: This archetype has never broken out in Historic, but Reckless Ringleader is a sweet *Jumpstart: Historic Horizons* addition—giving [Anax, Hardened in the Forge](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Anax%2C+Hardened+in+the+Forge) or [Goblin Chainwhirler](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Chainwhirler) haste can provide a lot of burst damage.

**Izzet Delver (1 player)**: It's basically Izzet Phoenix but with [Delver of Secrets](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets) and [Dreadhorde Arcanist](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dreadhorde+Arcanist) instead of [Arclight Phoenix](https://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arclight+Phoenix).


Watch Now!

Follow along the latest updates and watch the [Innistrad Championship](https://magic.gg/events/innistrad-championship), December 3–5, to see which deck comes out on top!
